## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of concentration change dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t. Classical rate laws typically depend on powers of concentration, but explicit time dependence may arise from integrated expressions of other coupled species or time-dependent external conditions.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order decay: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, first-order reaction)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of same species)
- nth-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (generalized power-law kinetics)
- Mixed order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (reaction with constant source/sink)
- Second-order with second species as function of time: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (pseudo-rate law with coupled species)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse first-order reaction near equilibrium)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme kinetics / saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * A) (autocatalytic reaction mechanism)
- Competitive inhibition form: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (substrate inhibition kinetics)
- Linear time-dependent rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * t) (time-varying rate coefficient)
- Product-inhibited kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + c2 * t) (product buildup inhibition, product ~ t)
- Coupled exponential decay: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A * exp(c2 * t) (coupled two-species system)
- Power-law with time: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (fractal or dispersive kinetics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- In closed chemical systems, dA/dt typically depends on negative powers or products of A, reflecting consumption stoichiometry
- Explicit time dependence in rate expressions often signals that another coupled species concentration has been substituted via its integrated form (e.g., B(t) = B0*exp(-k*t))
- Rational functions of A (e.g., A/(K+A)) indicate enzyme-like saturation where binding sites become limiting
- Quadratic or higher polynomial dependence on A suggests multi-molecular reaction steps or autocatalysis
- If dA/dt is proportional to A*(c-A), this indicates logistic-type autocatalytic growth with a carrying capacity from conservation laws
- Fractional power dependence on time (t**c) arises in dispersive kinetics on heterogeneous surfaces
- Products of A and functions of t often indicate bimolecular reactions where one reactant follows a known time trajectory
- Sign of the rate expression encodes whether A is a reactant (negative dA/dt) or product (positive dA/dt)
